<p><b>Richard Starkey</b>, <span style="font-size:85%;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Member of the Order of the British Empire">MBE</a></span> (born 7 July 1940), better known by his stage name <b>Ringo Starr</b>, is an English drummer, singer, songwriter, and actor who gained worldwide fame as the drummer for <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>. On most of the band's albums, he sang lead vocals for one song, including "<a href="/wiki/With_a_Little_Help_from_My_Friends" title="With a Little Help from My Friends">With a Little Help from My Friends</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(song)" title="Yellow Submarine (song)">Yellow Submarine</a>" and their <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Act_Naturally" title="Act Naturally">Act Naturally</a>". He also wrote the Beatles' songs "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Pass_Me_By" title="Don't Pass Me By">Don't Pass Me By</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Octopus%27s_Garden" title="Octopus's Garden">Octopus's Garden</a>", and is credited as a co-writer of others, such as "<a href="/wiki/What_Goes_On_(Beatles_song)" title="What Goes On (Beatles song)">What Goes On</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flying_(Beatles_song)" title="Flying (Beatles song)">Flying</a>".</p>
<p>Starr was twice afflicted by life-threatening illnesses during his childhood, and as a result of prolonged hospitalisations, fell behind scholastically. In 1955, he entered the workforce and briefly held a position with <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a> before securing an <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprenticeship</a> at a Liverpool equipment manufacturer. Soon afterwards, he became interested in the UK <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a> craze, developing a fervent admiration for the <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">genre</a>. In 1957, he cofounded his first band, the Eddie Clayton Skiffle Group, which earned several prestigious local bookings before the fad succumbed to American <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> by early 1958.</p>
<p>When the Beatles formed in 1960, Starr was a member of another <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> group, <a href="/wiki/Rory_Storm#Rory_Storm_and_the_Hurricanes" title="Rory Storm">Rory Storm and the Hurricanes</a>. After achieving moderate success with that band in the UK and <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, he quit the Hurricanes and joined the Beatles in August 1962, replacing <a href="/wiki/Pete_Best" title="Pete Best">Pete Best</a>. Starr played key roles in <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_film" title="The Beatles in film">The Beatles' films</a> and appeared in numerous others. After <a href="/wiki/Break-up_of_the_Beatles" title="Break-up of the Beatles">the band's break-up</a> in 1970, he released several successful singles including the US number four hit "<a href="/wiki/It_Don%27t_Come_Easy" title="It Don't Come Easy">It Don't Come Easy</a>", and number ones "<a href="/wiki/Photograph_(Ringo_Starr_song)" title="Photograph (Ringo Starr song)">Photograph"</a> and "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Sixteen" title="You're Sixteen">You're Sixteen</a>". In 1972, he released his most successful UK single, "<a href="/wiki/Back_Off_Boogaloo" title="Back Off Boogaloo">Back Off Boogaloo</a>", which peaked at number two. He achieved commercial and critical success with his 1973 album <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_(album)" title="Ringo (album)">Ringo</a></i>, which was a top ten release in both the UK and the US. He has been featured in a number of documentaries and hosted television shows. He also narrated the first two seasons of the children's television series <i><a href="/wiki/Thomas_%26_Friends" title="Thomas &amp; Friends">Thomas &amp; Friends</a></i> and portrayed "Mr Conductor" during the first season of the <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> children's television series <i><a href="/wiki/Shining_Time_Station" title="Shining Time Station">Shining Time Station</a></i>. Since 1989, he has successfully toured with twelve variations of <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr_%26_His_All-Starr_Band" title="Ringo Starr &amp; His All-Starr Band">Ringo Starr &amp; His All-Starr Band</a>.</p>
<p>Starr's creative contribution to music has received praise from drummers such as <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>, who described him as "a great musician",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_2011_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_2011-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Smith_(musician)" title="Steve Smith (musician)">Steve Smith</a>, who commented: "Before Ringo, drum stars were measured by their soloing ability and virtuosity. Ringo's popularity brought forth a new paradigm ... we started to see the drummer as an equal participant in the compositional aspect ... His parts are so signature to the songs that you can listen to a Ringo drum part without the rest of the music and still identify the song."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAS_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-PAS-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> readers named Starr the fifth-greatest drummer of all time. Starr will be inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> on April 18, 2015.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1940.E2.80.9356:_Early_life">1940–56: Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:9_Madryn_Street,_Liverpool_(6).JPG"><img alt="A colour photograph of a shabby looking, red bricked house with boarded up windows and doors" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3456" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/9_Madryn_Street%2C_Liverpool_%286%29.JPG/170px-9_Madryn_Street%2C_Liverpool_%286%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/9_Madryn_Street%2C_Liverpool_%286%29.JPG/255px-9_Madryn_Street%2C_Liverpool_%286%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/9_Madryn_Street%2C_Liverpool_%286%29.JPG/340px-9_Madryn_Street%2C_Liverpool_%286%29.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:9_Madryn_Street,_Liverpool_(6).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr's birthplace in Madryn Street, <a href="/wiki/Dingle,_Liverpool" title="Dingle, Liverpool">Dingle, Liverpool</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Richard Starkey was born on 7 July 1940, at 9 Madryn Street, in <a href="/wiki/Dingle,_Liverpool" title="Dingle, Liverpool">Dingle, Liverpool</a>. He is the only child of confectioners Elsie (née Gleave) and Richard Starkey, Sr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>nb 1<span>]</span></a></sup> Elsie enjoyed singing and dancing, a hobby that she shared with her husband, an avid fan of <a href="/wiki/Swing_(dance)" title="Swing (dance)">swing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332.E2.80.93333_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332.E2.80.93333-8"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to the birth of their son, whom they nicknamed "Ritchie", the couple had spent much of their free time on the local ballroom circuit, but soon after his birth their regular outings ended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005333.E2.80.93334_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005333.E2.80.93334-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Elsie adopted an overprotective approach to raising her son that bordered on fixation. Subsequently, "Big Ritchie", as Starkey's father became known, lost interest in his family, choosing instead to spend long hours drinking and dancing in pubs, sometimes for several consecutive days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005333.E2.80.93334_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005333.E2.80.93334-9"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1944, in an effort to reduce their housing costs, his family moved to another neighbourhood in the Dingle, <a href="/wiki/10_Admiral_Grove" title="10 Admiral Grove">10 Admiral Grove</a>; soon afterwards, his parents separated, and they divorced within the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Starkey later stated that he has "no real memories" of his father, who made little effort to bond with him, visiting as few as three times thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Elsie found it difficult to survive on her ex-husband's support payments of thirty shillings a week, so she took on several menial jobs cleaning houses before securing a position as a local barmaid, an occupation that she enjoyed for twelve years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005334.E2.80.93335_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005334.E2.80.93335-12"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg"><img alt="A colour photo of a white and pink cladded house" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2288" data-file-width="1712" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg/170px-Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg/255px-Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg/340px-Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr%27s_Home_Admiral_Grove_10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr's childhood residence at <a href="/wiki/10_Admiral_Grove" title="10 Admiral Grove">10 Admiral Grove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dingle,_Liverpool" title="Dingle, Liverpool">Dingle, Liverpool</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At age six Starkey developed <a href="/wiki/Appendicitis" title="Appendicitis">appendicitis</a>. Following a routine <a href="/wiki/Appendectomy" title="Appendectomy">appendectomy</a> he contracted <a href="/wiki/Peritonitis" title="Peritonitis">peritonitis</a>, causing him to fall into a coma that lasted for three days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> His recovery spanned twelve months, which he spent away from his family at Liverpool's Myrtle Street <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_hospital" title="Children's hospital">Children's hospital</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon his discharge in May 1948, his mother allowed him to stay home, causing him to miss school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005337_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005337-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> At age eight, he remained <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">illiterate</a>, with a poor grasp of mathematics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005337_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005337-15"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> His lack of education contributed to a feeling of alienation at school, which resulted in him regularly <a href="/wiki/Truancy" title="Truancy">playing truant</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sefton_Park" title="Sefton Park">Sefton Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> After several years of twice weekly tutoring from his surrogate sister and neighbour, Marie Maguire Crawford, Starkey had nearly caught up to his peers academically, but in 1953, he contracted <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and was admitted to a <a href="/wiki/Sanatorium" title="Sanatorium">sanatorium</a>, where he remained for two years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> During his stay the medical staff made an effort to stimulate motor activity and relieve boredom by encouraging their patients to join the hospital band, leading to his first exposure to a percussion instrument; a makeshift <a href="/wiki/Percussion_mallet" title="Percussion mallet">mallet</a> made from a cotton <a href="/wiki/Bobbin" title="Bobbin">bobbin</a> that he used to strike the cabinets next to his bed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon afterwards, he grew increasingly interested in drumming, receiving a copy of the <a href="/wiki/Alyn_Ainsworth" title="Alyn Ainsworth">Alyn Ainsworth</a> song "Bedtime for Drums" as a convalescence gift from Crawford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005339_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005339-19"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Starkey commented: "I was in the hospital band ... That's where I really started playing. I never wanted anything else from there on ... My grandparents gave me a mandolin and a banjo, but I didn't want them. My grandfather gave me a harmonica ... we had a piano – nothing. Only the drums."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200036_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Beatles200036-20"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starkey attended St Silas, a <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> primary school near his house where his classmates nicknamed him "<a href="/wiki/Lazarus_of_Bethany" title="Lazarus of Bethany">Lazarus</a>", and later Dingle Vale <a href="/wiki/Secondary_modern_school" title="Secondary modern school">Secondary modern school</a>, where he showed an aptitude for art and drama, as well as practical subjects including mechanics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result of the prolonged hospitalisations, he fell behind his peers scholastically and was ineligible for the <a href="/wiki/Eleven_plus_exam" title="Eleven plus exam">11-plus</a> qualifying examination required for attendance at a <a href="/wiki/Grammar_school" title="Grammar school">grammar school</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200523_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200523-22"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> On 17 April 1953, Starkey's mother married Harry Graves, an ex-Londoner who had moved to Liverpool following the failure of his first marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Graves, an impassioned fan of <a href="/wiki/Big_band" title="Big band">big band</a> music and their vocalists, introduced Starkey to recordings by <a href="/wiki/Dinah_Shore" title="Dinah Shore">Dinah Shore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Vaughan" title="Sarah Vaughan">Sarah Vaughan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Billy_Daniels" title="Billy Daniels">Billy Daniels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005340_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005340-24"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Graves stated that he and "Ritchie" never had an unpleasant exchange between them; Starkey later commented: "He was great ... I learned gentleness from Harry."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009146_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009146-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> After the extended hospital stay following Starkey's recovery from tuberculosis, he did not return to school, preferring instead to stay at home and listen to music while playing along by beating <a href="/wiki/Biscuit_tin" title="Biscuit tin">biscuit tins</a> with sticks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005336.E2.80.93339_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005336.E2.80.93339-26"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Beatles biographer <a href="/wiki/Bob_Spitz" title="Bob Spitz">Bob Spitz</a> described Starkey's upbringing as "a <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Dickensian</a> chronicle of misfortune".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Houses in the area were "poorly ventilated, postage-stamp-sized ... patched together by crumbling plaster walls, with a rear door that opened onto an <a href="/wiki/Outhouse" title="Outhouse">outhouse</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Crawford commented: "Like all of the families who lived in the Dingle, he was part of an ongoing struggle to survive."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The children who lived there spent much of their time at <a href="/wiki/Princes_Park,_Liverpool" title="Princes Park, Liverpool">Princes Park</a>, escaping the soot-filled air of their coal-fuelled neighbourhood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005332-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Adding to their difficult circumstances, violent crime was an almost constant concern for people living in one of the oldest and poorest inner-city districts in Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Starkey later commented: "You kept your head down, your eyes open, and you didn't get in anybody's way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005335_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005335-29"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After his return home from the sanatorium in late 1955, Starkey entered the UK workforce, but lacking motivation and discipline, his initial attempts at gainful employment proved unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> In an effort to secure himself some warm clothes, he briefly held a position at <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a>, who supplied their employees with suits. They gave him a hat, but no uniform, and unable to pass the <a href="/wiki/Physical_examination" title="Physical examination">physical examination</a>, he was laid off and granted <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_benefits" title="Unemployment benefits">unemployment benefits</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> He then found work as a waiter serving drinks on a day boat that travelled from Liverpool to North Wales, but his fear of <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> into military service led him to quit the job, not wanting to give the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> the impression that he was suitable for seafaring work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> In mid-1956, Graves secured Starkey a position as an apprentice <a href="/wiki/Machinist" title="Machinist">machinist</a> at a Liverpool equipment manufacturer. While working at the facility Starkey befriended Roy Trafford, and the two bonded over their shared interest in music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> Trafford introduced him to <a href="/wiki/Skiffle" title="Skiffle">skiffle</a>, and he quickly became a fervent admirer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1957.E2.80.9361:_First_bands">1957–61: First bands</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rory_Storm" title="Rory Storm">Rory Storm</a></div>
<p>Soon after Trafford piqued Starkey's interest in skiffle, the two began rehearsing songs in the manufacturing plant's cellar during their lunch breaks. Trafford recalled: "I played a guitar, and [Ritchie] just made a noise on a box ... Sometimes, he just slapped a biscuit tin with some keys, or banged on the backs of chairs."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341-33"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The pair were joined by Starkey's neighbour and co-worker, the guitarist Eddie Miles, forming the Eddie Miles Band, later renamed Eddie Clayton and the <a href="/wiki/Clayton_Square_Shopping_Centre" title="Clayton Square Shopping Centre">Clayton Squares</a> after a Liverpool landmark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341.E2.80.93342_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005341.E2.80.93342-34"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The band performed popular skiffle songs such as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_Island_Line_(song)" title="Rock Island Line (song)">Rock Island Line</a>" and "Walking Cane", with Starkey raking a <a href="/wiki/Thimble" title="Thimble">thimble</a> across a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washboard_as_a_musical_instrument" title="Washboard as a musical instrument">washboard</a>, creating primitive, driving rhythms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005342_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005342-35"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Starkey enjoyed dancing as his parents had years earlier, and he and Trafford briefly took dance lessons at two schools. Though the lessons were short-lived, they provided Starkey and Trafford with an introduction that allowed them to dance competently while enjoying nights out on the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005342_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005342-35"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On Christmas Day 1957, Graves gave Starkey a second-hand drum kit consisting of a <a href="/wiki/Snare_drum" title="Snare drum">snare drum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bass_drum" title="Bass drum">bass drum</a> and a makeshift <a href="/wiki/Cymbal" title="Cymbal">cymbal</a> fashioned from an old rubbish bin lid. Although basic and crude, the kit facilitated his progression as a musician while increasing the commercial potential of the Eddie Clayton band, who went on to book several prestigious local gigs before the skiffle craze faded in early 1958 as American <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> became popular in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1959, Starkey joined <a href="/wiki/Rory_Storm" title="Rory Storm">Al Caldwell</a>'s Texans, a skiffle group who were looking for someone with a proper drum kit so that the group could transition from one of Liverpool's best-known skiffle acts to a full-fledged rock and roll band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>nb 2<span>]</span></a></sup> They had begun playing local clubs as the Raging Texans, then Jet Storm and the Raging Texans before settling on Rory Storm and the Hurricanes soon before recruiting Starkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> About this time he adopted the stage name Ringo Starr; derived from the rings he wore and also because it implied a country western influence. His drum solos were billed as <i>Starr Time</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By early 1960 the Hurricanes had become one of Liverpool's leading bands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> In May, they were offered a three-month residency at a <a href="/wiki/Butlins" title="Butlins">Butlins</a> <a href="/wiki/Holiday_camp" title="Holiday camp">holiday camp</a> in Wales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199258_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199258-43"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Although initially reluctant to accept the residency and end his five-year machinist apprenticeship that he had begun four years earlier, Starr eventually agreed to the arrangement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The Butlins gig led to other opportunities for the band, including an unpleasant tour of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">US Air Force</a> bases in France about which Starr commented: "The French don't like the British; at least I didn't like them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009150_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009150-45"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The Hurricanes became so successful that when initially offered a highly coveted residency in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, they turned it down due to their prior commitment with Butlins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> They eventually accepted, joining <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Koschmider" title="Bruno Koschmider">Bruno Koschmider</a> '​s <a href="/wiki/Kaiserkeller" title="Kaiserkeller">Kaiserkeller</a> on 1 October 1960, where Starr first met the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Storm's Hurricanes were given top-billing over the Beatles, who also received less pay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr performed with the Beatles during a few stand-in engagements while in Hamburg. On 15 October 1960, he drummed with <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>, recording with them for the first time while backing Hurricanes singer Lu Walters on the <a href="/wiki/George_Gershwin" title="George Gershwin">George Gershwin</a> <a href="/wiki/Aria" title="Aria">aria</a> "<a href="/wiki/Summertime_(song)" title="Summertime (song)">Summertime</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>nb 3<span>]</span></a></sup> During Starr's first stay in Hamburg he also met <a href="/wiki/Tony_Sheridan" title="Tony Sheridan">Tony Sheridan</a>, who valued his drumming abilities to the point of asking Starr to leave the Hurricanes and join his band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="1962.E2.80.9370:_The_Beatles">1962–70: The Beatles</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Fabs.JPG"><img alt="Four greyscale images of the young Beatles with &quot;mop-top&quot; haircuts. Lennon (top left) is looking towards the left of the frame (his right), with exposed teeth. McCartney (top right) is facing forward with an opened mouth. Harrison (bottom left) has his right arm raised and his tongue stuck out slightly as if licking his lips. Starr's teeth are visible, and his left eye is closed as if winking. All four are dressed in white shirts, black ties, and dark coats." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1110" data-file-width="1110" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_Fabs.JPG/220px-The_Fabs.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_Fabs.JPG/330px-The_Fabs.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_Fabs.JPG/440px-The_Fabs.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Fabs.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr (bottom right) with Lennon (top left), McCartney (top right) and Harrison (bottom left), arriving in New York City, 1964</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Starr quit Rory Storm and the Hurricanes in January 1962 and briefly joined Sheridan in Hamburg before returning to the Hurricanes for a third season at Butlins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>nb 4<span>]</span></a></sup> On 14 August, Lennon asked Starr to join the Beatles; he accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-56"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> On 16 August, Beatles manager <a href="/wiki/Brian_Epstein" title="Brian Epstein">Brian Epstein</a> fired their drummer, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Best" title="Pete Best">Pete Best</a>, who recalled: "He said 'I've got some bad news for you. The boys want you out and Ringo in ... He said [Beatles producer] <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a> wasn't too pleased with my playing [and] the boys thought I didn't fit in."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009137_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009137-57"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr first performed as a member of the band on 18 August 1962, at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horticultural_Society" title="Horticultural Society">Horticultural Society</a> dance at <a href="/wiki/Port_Sunlight" title="Port Sunlight">Port Sunlight</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> After his appearance at the <a href="/wiki/The_Cavern_Club" title="The Cavern Club">Cavern Club</a> the following day, Best fans, upset by his firing, held vigils outside his house and at the club shouting "Pete forever! Ringo never!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004110_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004110-54"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Harrison received a black eye from one of the upset fans and Epstein, whose car tyres they had flattened in anger, temporarily hired a bodyguard to ensure his safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr's first recording session as a member of the Beatles took place on 4 September 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-56"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> He stated that Martin had thought that he "was crazy and couldn't play ... because I was trying to play the percussion and the drums at the same time, we were just a four piece band".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett2001126_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett2001126-60"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> For their second recording session with Starr, which took place on 11 September 1962, Martin replaced him with session drummer <a href="/wiki/Andy_White_(drummer)" title="Andy White (drummer)">Andy White</a> while recording takes for what would be the <a href="/wiki/A-side_and_B-side" title="A-side and B-side">two sides</a> of the Beatles' first single, "<a href="/wiki/Love_Me_Do" title="Love Me Do">Love Me Do</a>", backed with "<a href="/wiki/P.S._I_Love_You_(Beatles_song)" title="P.S. I Love You (Beatles song)">P.S. I Love You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004367.E2.80.93368_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004367.E2.80.93368-61"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr played tambourine on "Love Me Do" and maracas on "P.S. I Love You".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-56"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Concerned about his status in the Beatles, he thought: "That's the end, they're doing a Pete Best on me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009163_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009163-62"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> Martin later clarified: "I simply didn't know what Ringo was like and I wasn't prepared to take any risks."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200596_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200596-63"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>nb 5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By November 1962 Starr had been accepted by Beatles fans, who were now calling for him to sing songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200589.2C_147_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200589.2C_147-65"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon afterwards, he began receiving an amount of fanmail equal to that of the others, which helped to secure his position within the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005105_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005105-66"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr considered himself fortunate to be on the same "wavelength" as the other Beatles: "I had to be, or I wouldn't have lasted. I had to join them as people [<i>sic</i>] as well as [as] a drummer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200594_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200594-67"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> He was given a small percentage of Lennon and McCartney's publishing company, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Songs" title="Northern Songs">Northern Songs</a>, but he derived his primary income during this period from a one-quarter share of Beatles Ltd, a corporation financed by the band's net concert earnings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005105_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005105-66"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> He commented on the nature of his lifestyle after having achieved success with the Beatles: "I lived in nightclubs for three years. It used to be a non-stop party."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005112_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005112-68"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Like his father Starr became well known for his late-night dancing and he received considerable praise for his skills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005112_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005112-68"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During 1963, the Beatles enjoyed increasing popularity in Britain. In January, their second single, "<a href="/wiki/Please_Please_Me_(song)" title="Please Please Me (song)">Please Please Me</a>", followed "Love Me Do" into the UK charts and a successful television appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/Thank_Your_Lucky_Stars_(TV_series)" title="Thank Your Lucky Stars (TV series)">Thank Your Lucky Stars</a></i> earned them favourable reviews, leading to a boost in sales and radio play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199288_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199288-69"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the year, the phenomenon known as <a href="/wiki/Beatlemania" title="Beatlemania">Beatlemania</a> had spread throughout the country, and by February 1964 the Beatles had become an international success, performing on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ed_Sullivan_Show" title="The Ed Sullivan Show">The Ed Sullivan Show</a></i> to a record 73 million viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199293.2C_136.E2.80.93137_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199293.2C_136.E2.80.93137-70"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr commented: "In the states I know I went over well. It knocked me out to see and hear the kids waving for me. I'd made it as a personality ... Our appeal ... is that we're ordinary lads."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> He was a source of inspiration for several songs written at the time, including <a href="/wiki/Penny_Valentine" title="Penny Valentine">Penny Valentine</a>'s "I Want to Kiss Ringo Goodbye" and <a href="/wiki/Rolf_Harris" title="Rolf Harris">Rolf Harris</a>'s "Ringo for President".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005122_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005122-72"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1964, "I love Ringo" lapel pins outsold all other Beatles merchandising.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005122_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005122-72"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> During live performances, the Beatles continued the <i>Starr Time</i> routine that had been popular among his fans: Lennon would place a microphone in front of Starr's kit in preparation for his spotlight moment and audiences would erupt in screams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005123_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005123-73"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> When the Beatles made their film debut in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(film)" title="A Hard Day's Night (film)">A Hard Day's Night</a></i>, Starr garnered much praise from critics, who considered both his delivery of deadpan one-liners and his non-speaking scenes highlights of the movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005124.E2.80.93125_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005124.E2.80.93125-74"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The extended non-speaking sequences had to be arranged by director <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lester" title="Richard Lester">Richard Lester</a> due to Starr's lack of sleep the previous night, Starr commented: "Because I'd been drinking all night I was incapable of saying a line."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005125_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005125-75"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Epstein attributed Starr's acclaim to "the little man's quaintness".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005124_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005124-76"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> After the release of the Beatles' second feature film, <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(film)" title="Help! (film)">Help!</a></i> (1965), Starr won a <i>Melody Maker</i> poll against his fellow Beatles for his performance as the central character in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005148_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005148-77"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> in 1964, Lennon explained that Starr had filled in with the Beatles when Best was ill; Starr replied: "[Best] took little pills to make him ill".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005128_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005128-78"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon after Starr made the comment, a provoked Best filed a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libel" title="Libel">libel</a> suit against him that lasted for four years before the court reached an undisclosed settlement in Best's favour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005127.E2.80.93128_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005127.E2.80.93128-79"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> In June, the Beatles were scheduled to tour Denmark, the Netherlands, Asia, Australia and New Zealand, but Starr became ill the day before the start of the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992160.E2.80.93161_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992160.E2.80.93161-80"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Stricken with a high-grade fever, <a href="/wiki/Pharyngitis" title="Pharyngitis">pharyngitis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tonsillitis" title="Tonsillitis">tonsillitis</a>, he was admitted to a local hospital where he briefly stayed followed by several days of recuperation at home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005128.E2.80.93130_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005128.E2.80.93130-81"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> During this time, Starr was temporarily replaced for five concert dates by 24-year-old session drummer <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Nicol" title="Jimmie Nicol">Jimmie Nicol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002132_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBabiuk2002132-82"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr was discharged from the hospital, and he rejoined the band in Melbourne on 15 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992160.E2.80.93163_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992160.E2.80.93163-83"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>nb 6<span>]</span></a></sup> He later admitted that he feared he would be permanently replaced during his illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> In August, when the Beatles were introduced to <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>, Starr was the first to try a cannabis cigarette offered to the band by Dylan, whereas Lennon, McCartney and Harrison were hesitant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 February 1965, Starr married <a href="/wiki/Maureen_Starkey_Tigrett" title="Maureen Starkey Tigrett">Maureen Cox</a>, whom he had first met in 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004333.E2.80.93334_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004333.E2.80.93334-89"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> By this time the negative aspects of Beatlemania had reached a peak for him, who after having received a telephoned death threat before a show in Montreal resorted to positioning his cymbals vertically in an attempt to provide protection from would-be assassins. The constant pressure of the Beatles' fame impacted their live performances; Starr commented: "We were turning into such bad musicians ... there was no groove to it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005139.E2.80.93140_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005139.E2.80.93140-90"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> He was also feeling increasingly isolated from the musical activities of his bandmates, who were moving past the traditional boundaries of rock music into territory that often did not require his accompaniment; during recording sessions he spent countless hours playing cards with their road manager <a href="/wiki/Neil_Aspinall" title="Neil Aspinall">Neil Aspinall</a> and roadie <a href="/wiki/Mal_Evans" title="Mal Evans">Mal Evans</a> while the other Beatles perfected tracks without him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005147_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005147-91"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> In a letter published in <i>Melody Maker</i>, a fan asked the Beatles to let Starr sing more; he replied: "[I am] quite happy with my one little track on each album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005147_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005147-91"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 1966, the Beatles released <i><a href="/wiki/Revolver_(Beatles_album)" title="Revolver (Beatles album)">Revolver</a></i>, their seventh UK LP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992350-92"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> The album included the song "<a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(song)" title="Yellow Submarine (song)">Yellow Submarine</a>", which was the only British number one single with Starr as the lead singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005159_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005159-93"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that month and owing to the increasing pressures of touring, the Beatles gave their final concert, a 30-minute performance at San Francisco '​s <a href="/wiki/Candlestick_Park" title="Candlestick Park">Candlestick Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr commented: "We gave up touring at the right time. Four years of Beatlemania were enough for anyone."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005152_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005152-95"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> By December, he had moved into an upscale estate on three acres in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_George%27s_Hill" title="Saint George's Hill">Saint George's Hill</a> called <a href="/wiki/Sunny_Heights" title="Sunny Heights">Sunny Heights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005142.E2.80.93144_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005142.E2.80.93144-96"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Although he had adorned the house with many of the finest luxuries available at the time, including numerous televisions, light machines, film projectors and stereo equipment, a <a href="/wiki/Billiard_table" title="Billiard table">billiard table</a>, <a href="/wiki/Go-kart" title="Go-kart">go-kart</a> track and a bar named the Flying Cow, he did not include a drum kit, he explained: "When we don't record, I don't play".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005143.E2.80.93144_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005143.E2.80.93144-97"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For the Beatles' seminal 1967 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i>, Starr sang lead vocals on the <a href="/wiki/Lennon%E2%80%93McCartney" title="Lennon–McCartney">Lennon–McCartney</a> composition "<a href="/wiki/With_a_Little_Help_from_My_Friends" title="With a Little Help from My Friends">With a Little Help from My Friends</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005159.E2.80.93161.2C_179_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005159.E2.80.93161.2C_179-98"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Although the Beatles had enjoyed widespread commercial and critical success with <i>Sgt. Pepper</i>, the long hours they spent recording the LP contributed to Starr's increased feeling of alienation within the band, he commented: "[It] wasn't our best album. That was the peak for everyone else, but for me it was a bit like being a session musician ... They more or less direct me in the style I can play."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005160.E2.80.93161_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005160.E2.80.93161-99"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>nb 7<span>]</span></a></sup> His inability to compose new material led to his input being minimised during recording sessions; he often found himself relegated to adding minor percussion effects to songs by McCartney, Lennon and Harrison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005161.E2.80.93162_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005161.E2.80.93162-102"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> During his down-time Starr worked on his guitar playing; he commented: "I jump into chords that no one seems to get into. Most of the stuff I write is twelve-bar".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005161_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005161-103"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Epstein's death in August 1967 left the Beatles without management; Starr remarked: "[It was] a strange time for us, when it's someone who've relied on in the business, where we never got involved."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005166_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005166-104"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon afterwards, the band began an ill-fated film project, <i><a href="/wiki/Magical_Mystery_Tour_(film)" title="Magical Mystery Tour (film)">Magical Mystery Tour</a></i>. Starr's growing interest in photography at the time lead to his billing as the movie's Director of Photography, and his participation in the film's editing was matched only by McCartney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005166.E2.80.93168_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005166.E2.80.93168-105"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1968, Starr became the first Beatle to sing during another artist's show without the other three present. He sang the <a href="/wiki/Buck_Owens" title="Buck Owens">Buck Owens</a> hit "<a href="/wiki/Act_Naturally" title="Act Naturally">Act Naturally</a>", and performed a duet with <a href="/wiki/Cilla_Black" title="Cilla Black">Cilla Black</a>, "Do you Like Me Just a Little Bit?" on her <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> television programme, <i>Cilla</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005175.E2.80.93176_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005175.E2.80.93176-106"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year <a href="/wiki/Apple_Records" title="Apple Records">Apple Records</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)" title="The Beatles (album)">The Beatles</a></i>, commonly known as the <i>White Album</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007510_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007510-107"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Creative inspiration for the double-LP came in part from the band's recent interactions with the <a href="/wiki/Maharishi_Mahesh_Yogi" title="Maharishi Mahesh Yogi">Maharishi Mahesh Yogi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000705.E2.80.93706_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000705.E2.80.93706-108"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> While attending an intermediate course at his <a href="/wiki/Ashram" title="Ashram">ashram</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rishikesh" title="Rishikesh">Rishikesh</a>, India, they enjoyed one of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_India" title="The Beatles in India">their most prolific writing periods</a>, composing most of the album's songs there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2000108.E2.80.93109_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2000108.E2.80.93109-109"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite leaving after ten days, Starr completed his first recorded Beatles song, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Pass_Me_By" title="Don't Pass Me By">Don't Pass Me By</a>", while in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>nb 8<span>]</span></a></sup> During the recording of the <i>White Album</i>, relations within the band became openly divisive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992283.E2.80.93304_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992283.E2.80.93304-114"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> As the sessions progressed, their collective group dynamic began to decay; at times only one or two Beatles were involved in the recording for a track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005182.E2.80.93184_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005182.E2.80.93184-115"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr had grown weary of McCartney's increasingly overbearing approach and Lennon's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Passive-aggressive_behaviour" title="Passive-aggressive behaviour">passive-aggressive behaviour</a>, which was exacerbated by Starr's resentment of <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a> '​s near constant presence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005182.E2.80.93184_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005182.E2.80.93184-115"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> After one particularly difficult session during which McCartney had harshly criticised his drumming, he quit the band for two weeks, taking a holiday with his family in <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a> on a boat loaned by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">Peter Sellers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> During a lunch break the chef served octopus, which Starr refused to eat. A subsequent conversation with the ship's captain regarding the behaviours of the animal served as the inspiration for his <i><a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road" title="Abbey Road">Abbey Road</a></i> composition, "<a href="/wiki/Octopus%27s_Garden" title="Octopus's Garden">Octopus's Garden</a>", which Starr wrote on guitar during the trip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> When he returned to the studio two weeks later, he discovered that his drum kit had been covered in flowers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992295.E2.80.93296_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992295.E2.80.93296-118"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite a temporary return to congenial relations during the completion of the <i>White Album</i>, production of the Beatles' fourth feature film, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Let_It_Be_(film)" title="Let It Be (film)">Let It Be</a></i>, and its <a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be" title="Let It Be">accompanying LP</a>, strained an already tenuous cohesion within the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005189.E2.80.93192_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005189.E2.80.93192-119"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> On 20 August 1969, the Beatles gathered for the final time at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> for a mixing session for "<a href="/wiki/I_Want_You_(She%27s_So_Heavy)" title="I Want You (She's So Heavy)">I Want You (She's So Heavy)</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992331_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992331-120"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Following a business meeting on 20 September 1969, Lennon told the others that <a href="/wiki/Break-up_of_the_Beatles" title="Break-up of the Beatles">he had quit the Beatles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_career">Solo career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Last_Waltz.jpg"><img alt="A black and white photo of about a dozen musicians performing on a stage." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="406" data-file-width="600" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/The_Last_Waltz.jpg/250px-The_Last_Waltz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/The_Last_Waltz.jpg/375px-The_Last_Waltz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/The_Last_Waltz.jpg/500px-The_Last_Waltz.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Last_Waltz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr, rear centre drumming with Bob Dylan and <a href="/wiki/The_Band" title="The Band">the Band</a>, November 1976</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 10 April 1970, McCartney publicly announced that he had quit the Beatles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992341.2C_349_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn1992341.2C_349-122"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr released two albums before the end of that year: <i><a href="/wiki/Sentimental_Journey_(Ringo_Starr_album)" title="Sentimental Journey (Ringo Starr album)">Sentimental Journey</a></i>, a UK number seven hit composed of his renditions of many pre-rock standards that included musical arrangements by <a href="/wiki/Quincy_Jones" title="Quincy Jones">Quincy Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Gibb" title="Maurice Gibb">Maurice Gibb</a>, George Martin and McCartney, and the country-inspired <i><a href="/wiki/Beaucoups_of_Blues" title="Beaucoups of Blues">Beaucoups of Blues</a></i>, engineered by <a href="/wiki/Scotty_Moore" title="Scotty Moore">Scotty Moore</a> and featuring renowned <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville</a> session musician <a href="/wiki/Pete_Drake" title="Pete Drake">Pete Drake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr played drums on Lennon's <i><a href="/wiki/John_Lennon/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band">John Lennon/Plastic Ono Band</a></i> (1970), Ono's <i><a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="Yoko Ono/Plastic Ono Band">Yoko Ono/Plastic Ono Band</a></i> (1970), and on Harrison's albums <i><a href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass" title="All Things Must Pass">All Things Must Pass</a></i> (1970) and <i><a href="/wiki/Living_in_the_Material_World" title="Living in the Material World">Living in the Material World</a></i> (1973).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1971, Starr participated in <a href="/wiki/The_Concert_for_Bangladesh" title="The Concert for Bangladesh">the Concert for Bangladesh</a>, organised by Harrison, and with him co-wrote the hit single "<a href="/wiki/It_Don%27t_Come_Easy" title="It Don't Come Easy">It Don't Come Easy</a>", which reached number four in both the US and the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The following year he released his most successful UK hit, "<a href="/wiki/Back_Off_Boogaloo" title="Back Off Boogaloo">Back Off Boogaloo</a>", which peaked at number two (US number nine).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year he made his directorial debut with the <a href="/wiki/T._Rex_(band)" title="T. Rex (band)">T. Rex</a> documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Born_to_Boogie" title="Born to Boogie">Born to Boogie</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200491.E2.80.9393_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200491.E2.80.9393-127"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>nb 9<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1973, he earned two number one hits in the US: "<a href="/wiki/Photograph_(Ringo_Starr_song)" title="Photograph (Ringo Starr song)">Photograph</a>", a UK number eight hit that was co-written with Harrison, and "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Sixteen" title="You're Sixteen">You're Sixteen</a>", written by the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Brothers" title="Sherman Brothers">Sherman Brothers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr's third million-selling single and his second US chart-topper, "You're Sixteen" was released in the UK in February 1974 where it peaked at number four in the charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004372_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004372-130"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1973, Starr released <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_(album)" title="Ringo (album)">Ringo</a></i>, a commercially successful album produced by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Perry" title="Richard Perry">Richard Perry</a> that featured writing and musical contributions from Harrison, Lennon and McCartney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004281.E2.80.93282_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004281.E2.80.93282-131"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The LP yielded the hit song "<a href="/wiki/Oh_My_My_(Ringo_Starr_song)" title="Oh My My (Ringo Starr song)">Oh My My</a>", a US number five that was Starr's fifth consecutive top-ten hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004260:_.22Oh_My_My.22_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004260:_.22Oh_My_My.22-132"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> The album reached number seven in the UK and number two in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Goodnight_Vienna" title="Goodnight Vienna">Goodnight Vienna</a></i> followed in 1974 and was also successful, reaching number eight in the US and number 30 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The album earned Starr a pair of top-ten hits with his cover of <a href="/wiki/The_Platters" title="The Platters">the Platters</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Only_You_(And_You_Alone)" title="Only You (And You Alone)">Only You (And You Alone)</a>", which peaked at number six in the US and number 28 in the UK, and "<a href="/wiki/No_No_Song" title="No No Song">No No Song</a>", which was a US number three and Starr's seventh consecutive top-ten hit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>nb 10<span>]</span></a></sup> During this period he became romantically involved with <a href="/wiki/Lynsey_de_Paul" title="Lynsey de Paul">Lynsey de Paul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004180.E2.80.93181_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004180.E2.80.93181-138"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> He played tambourine on a song she wrote and produced for <a href="/wiki/Vera_Lynn" title="Vera Lynn">Vera Lynn</a>, "Don't You Remember When", and he inspired another De Paul song, "If I Don't Get You the Next One Will", which she described as being about revenge after he missed a dinner appointment with her because he was asleep in his office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004180.E2.80.93181_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004180.E2.80.93181-138"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr founded the record label Ring O'Records in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004279.E2.80.93280_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004279.E2.80.93280-139"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> The company signed eleven artists and released fifteen singles and five albums between 1975 and 1978, including works by <a href="/wiki/David_Hentschel" title="David Hentschel">David Hentschel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graham_Bonnet" title="Graham Bonnet">Graham Bonnet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rab_Noakes" title="Rab Noakes">Rab Noakes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004280_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004280-140"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> The commercial impact of Starr's recording career subsequently diminished, although he continued to record and remained a familiar celebrity presence. In 1976 Starr appeared as a guest in <a href="/wiki/The_Band" title="The Band">The Band</a>'s farewell concert, featured in the 1978 <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> documentary <a href="/wiki/The_Last_Waltz" title="The Last Waltz">The Last Waltz</a>. Also in 1976, <a href="/wiki/Polydor_Records" title="Polydor Records">Polydor Records</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo%27s_Rotogravure" title="Ringo's Rotogravure">Ringo's Rotogravure</a></i>, an album that featured compositions by McCartney, Lennon and Harrison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004295_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004295-141"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Although the album and its accompanying singles failed to chart in the UK, the LP produced two minor US hits, "<a href="/wiki/A_Dose_of_Rock_%27n%27_Roll" title="A Dose of Rock 'n' Roll">A Dose of Rock 'n' Roll</a>" (number 26) and a cover of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hey!_Baby" title="Hey! Baby">Hey! Baby</a>" (number 74), and achieved moderate sales, reaching a chart position of 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> This inspired Polydor to revamp Starr's formula; the results were a curious blend of disco and 1970s pop, <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_the_4th" title="Ringo the 4th">Ringo the 4th</a></i> (1977).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004294.E2.80.93295_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004294.E2.80.93295-143"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was a commercial disaster, failing to chart in the UK and peaking at number 162 in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1978 Starr released <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Boy_(Ringo_Starr_album)" title="Bad Boy (Ringo Starr album)">Bad Boy</a></i>; the album reached a disappointing number 129 in the US and failed to chart in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg"><img alt="Starr in his forties, wearing a grey jacket and a black shirt, standing behind a microphone and singing." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="974" data-file-width="1410" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg/220px-Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg/330px-Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg/440px-Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Princes_Trust.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr performing for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" title="Prince's Trust">Prince's Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>, England, 6 June 1987.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/Death_of_John_Lennon" title="Death of John Lennon">Lennon's murder</a> in 1980, Harrison modified the lyrics of a song he had originally written for Starr, "<a href="/wiki/All_Those_Years_Ago" title="All Those Years Ago">All Those Years Ago</a>", as a tribute to their former bandmate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009273_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009273-146"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> The track, which included vocal contributions from both Paul and <a href="/wiki/Linda_McCartney" title="Linda McCartney">Linda McCartney</a> and Starr's original drum part, peaked at number two in the US charts, and number 13 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>nb 11<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1981, Starr released <i><a href="/wiki/Stop_and_Smell_the_Roses" title="Stop and Smell the Roses">Stop and Smell the Roses</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004326.E2.80.93327_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004326.E2.80.93327-150"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> The LP contained the Harrison composition "Wrack My Brain", which reached number 38 in the US charts, but failed to chart in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> Lennon had offered a pair of songs for use on the album: "<a href="/wiki/Nobody_Told_Me" title="Nobody Told Me">Nobody Told Me</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Life_Begins_at_40" title="Life Begins at 40">Life Begins at 40</a>", but following his death, Starr did not feel comfortable recording them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004326.E2.80.93327_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004326.E2.80.93327-150"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon after the murder, Starr and his girlfriend <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bach" title="Barbara Bach">Barbara Bach</a> flew to New York City to be with Lennon's widow Yoko Ono.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005301_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005301-152"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From 1984 to 1986, Starr narrated the children's series <i><a href="/wiki/Thomas_%26_Friends" title="Thomas &amp; Friends">Thomas &amp; Friends</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Britt_Allcroft" title="Britt Allcroft">Britt Allcroft</a> production based on the books by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/W._V._Awdry" title="W. V. Awdry">Reverend W. Awdry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004322_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004322-153"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr also portrayed the character Mr. Conductor in the programme's American spin-off <i><a href="/wiki/Shining_Time_Station" title="Shining Time Station">Shining Time Station</a></i>, which debuted in 1989 on <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>. He left after the first season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004314_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004314-154"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1985, he performed with his son <a href="/wiki/Zak_Starkey" title="Zak Starkey">Zak</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Artists_United_Against_Apartheid" title="Artists United Against Apartheid">Artists United Against Apartheid</a> on the recording, <i><a href="/wiki/Sun_City_(song)" title="Sun City (song)">Sun City</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004328_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004328-155"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1987 Starr played drums on the song "<a href="/wiki/When_We_Was_Fab" title="When We Was Fab">When We Was Fab</a>", from Harrison's album <i><a href="/wiki/Cloud_Nine_(George_Harrison_album)" title="Cloud Nine (George Harrison album)">Cloud Nine</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009292_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDoggett2009292-156"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> The song, which was co-written by Harrison and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Lynne" title="Jeff Lynne">Jeff Lynne</a>, charted in the top 30 in both the UK and the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> The same year, Starr, Harrison and Lynne joined <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ray_Cooper" title="Ray Cooper">Ray Cooper</a> in a performance for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" title="Prince's Trust">Prince's Trust</a> charity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003304.E2.80.93305_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003304.E2.80.93305-158"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During October and November 1988, Starr and Bach attended a <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_detoxification" title="Alcohol detoxification">detox</a> clinic in <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson, Arizona</a>, each receiving a six-week treatment for alcoholism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004135_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004135-159"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>nb 12<span>]</span></a></sup> On 23 July 1989, <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr_%26_His_All-Starr_Band" title="Ringo Starr &amp; His All-Starr Band">Ringo Starr &amp; His All-Starr Band</a> gave their first performance to an audience of ten thousand in <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004136_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004136-162"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> The band consisted of Starr and a varying assortment of musicians who had been successful in their own right with popular songs at different times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry20047_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry20047-163"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The concerts interchanged Starr's singing, including selections of his Beatles and solo songs, with performances of each of the other artists' well-known material, the latter incorporating either Starr or another musician as drummer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry20047_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry20047-163"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span></h3>
<p>The first All-Starr excursion led to the release of <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr_and_His_All-Starr_Band" title="Ringo Starr and His All-Starr Band">Ringo Starr and His All-Starr Band</a></i> (1990), a compilation of live performances from the tour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005345_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005345-164"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same year, Starr recorded a version of the song "<a href="/wiki/I_Call_Your_Name" title="I Call Your Name">I Call Your Name</a>" for a television special marking the 10th anniversary of John Lennon's death and the 50th anniversary of Lennon's birth. The track, produced by Lynne, features a supergroup composed of Lynne, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Petty" title="Tom Petty">Tom Petty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Walsh" title="Joe Walsh">Joe Walsh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Keltner" title="Jim Keltner">Jim Keltner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004226_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004226-165"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The following year, Starr made a cameo appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Brush_with_Greatness" title="Brush with Greatness">Brush with Greatness</a>" and contributed an original song, "You Never Know", to the soundtrack of the <a href="/wiki/John_Hughes_(filmmaker)" title="John Hughes (filmmaker)">John Hughes</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Curly_Sue" title="Curly Sue">Curly Sue</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004315.E2.80.93316:_.22Brush_with_Greatness.22.3B_178:_.27.27Curly_Sue.27.27_and_.22You_Never_Know.22_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004315.E2.80.93316:_.22Brush_with_Greatness.22.3B_178:_.27.27Curly_Sue.27.27_and_.22You_Never_Know.22-166"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1992, Starr released his first studio album in nine years, <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Takes_Time" title="Time Takes Time">Time Takes Time</a></i>, which was produced by <a href="/wiki/Phil_Ramone" title="Phil Ramone">Phil Ramone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Was" title="Don Was">Don Was</a>, Lynne and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Asher" title="Peter Asher">Peter Asher</a> and featured guest appearances by various stars including <a href="/wiki/Brian_Wilson" title="Brian Wilson">Brian Wilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Nilsson" title="Harry Nilsson">Harry Nilsson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004334.E2.80.93337_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004334.E2.80.93337-167"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1994, Starr began a collaboration with the surviving former Beatles for the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_Anthology" title="The Beatles Anthology">Beatles Anthology</a></i> project. They recorded two new Beatles songs built around solo vocal and piano tapes recorded by Lennon and gave lengthy interviews about the Beatles' career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999286_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999286-168"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Released in December 1995, "<a href="/wiki/Free_as_a_Bird" title="Free as a Bird">Free as a Bird</a>" was the first new Beatles single since 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> In March 1996, they released a second single, "<a href="/wiki/Real_Love_(The_Beatles_song)" title="Real Love (The Beatles song)">Real Love</a>". Harrison refused to participate in the completion of a third song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr guested on two songs from McCartney's 1997 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Flaming_Pie" title="Flaming Pie">Flaming Pie</a></i>. McCartney had written a song about Starr's ex-wife Maureen, who died in 1994, called "Little Willow" and asked Starr if he would play on another song, "Beautiful Night".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004236:_.27.27Little_Willow.22.3B_83.E2.80.9384:_.22Beautiful_Night.22_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004236:_.27.27Little_Willow.22.3B_83.E2.80.9384:_.22Beautiful_Night.22-171"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> The day after the "Beautiful Night" session, the two recorded a jam session, which developed into another song, "Really Love You", notable for being the first official release ever credited to McCartney/Starkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004275_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004275-172"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1998, he released two albums on the <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Records" title="Mercury Records">Mercury</a> label. The studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Vertical_Man" title="Vertical Man">Vertical Man</a></i> marked the beginning of a nine-year partnership with <a href="/wiki/Mark_Hudson_(musician)" title="Mark Hudson (musician)">Mark Hudson</a>, who produced the album and, with his band the Roundheads, formed the core of the backing group for the album. In addition, many famous guests joined on various tracks, including Martin, McCartney and, in his final appearance on a Starr album, Harrison. Most of the songs were written by Starr and the band. Joe Walsh and the Roundheads joined Starr for his appearance on <i><a href="/wiki/VH1_Storytellers_(Ringo_Starr_album)" title="VH1 Storytellers (Ringo Starr album)">VH1 Storytellers</a></i>, which was released as an album under the same name.
