During the show, he performed greatest hits and new songs and told anecdotes relating to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004358_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004358-173"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr.jpg"><img alt="Starr is on stage with two guitarists and two microphones. He is wearing sunglasses and a black and silver T-shirt, and both of his arms are raised. His right arm forms a V-shaped peace symbol." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="251" data-file-width="373" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ringo_Starr.jpg/220px-Ringo_Starr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Ringo_Starr.jpg/330px-Ringo_Starr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/Ringo_Starr.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringo_Starr.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr on stage in New York City in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Starr was inducted into the Percussive Arts Society Hall of Fame in 2002, joining an elite group including <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Rich" title="Buddy Rich">Buddy Rich</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ludwig-Musser" title="Ludwig-Musser">William F. Ludwig, Sr., and William F. Ludwig, Jr.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> On 29 November 2002 (the first anniversary of Harrison's death), Starr performed "Photograph" and a cover of <a href="/wiki/Carl_Perkins" title="Carl Perkins">Carl Perkins</a>' "<a href="/wiki/Honey_Don%27t" title="Honey Don't">Honey Don't</a>" at the <i><a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a></i> held in the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2003138.E2.80.93139-175"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, Starr formed Pumkinhead Records with All-Starr Band member Mark Hudson.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> The label was not prolific, but their first signing was <a href="/wiki/Liam_Lynch_(musician)" title="Liam Lynch (musician)">Liam Lynch</a>, who produced a 2003 LP entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Fake_Songs" title="Fake Songs">Fake Songs</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004241_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004241-177"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr served as an honorary Santa Tracker and voice-over personality in 2003 and 2004 during the London stop in Father Christmas's annual Christmas Eve journey, as depicted in the annual <a href="/wiki/NORAD_Tracks_Santa" title="NORAD Tracks Santa">NORAD tracks Santa program</a>. According to NORAD officials, he was "a Starr in the east" who helped guide <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aerospace_Defense_Command" title="North American Aerospace Defense Command">North American Aerospace Defense Command</a>'s Santa-tracking tradition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27Starr.27_helps_NORAD_track_Santa_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27Starr.27_helps_NORAD_track_Santa-178"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2004_-_ringo_thankspage_thumb.jpg"><img alt='A colour photo of Starr, who is holding two fingers up in the style of a "peace sign". He is a wearing a dark beret, sunglasses and a grey windbreaker with several patches on the front.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="150" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/2004_-_ringo_thankspage_thumb.jpg" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2004_-_ringo_thankspage_thumb.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr as an <a href="/wiki/NORAD_Tracks_Santa" title="NORAD Tracks Santa">Honorary Santa Tracker</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, Liverpool's City Council announced plans to demolish Starr's birthplace, 9 Madryn Street, stating that it had "no historical significance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> The LCC later announced that the building would be taken apart brick by brick and preserved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr released <i><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_8" title="Liverpool 8">Liverpool 8</a></i> in 2008, an album produced by <a href="/wiki/David_A._Stewart" title="David A. Stewart">David A. Stewart</a>, Mark Hudson and Starr. Hudson was the initial producer of the recordings but was replaced by Stewart after a falling out with Starr. According to the journalist Peter Palmiere, the partnership between Hudson and Starr ended because of Starr's insistence on using synthesised sounds, for which Stewart is known, whereas Hudson wanted real guitars, pianos and strings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>nb 13<span>]</span></a></sup> On 10 October 2008, Starr posted a video on his website stating that he would not be signing autographs after 20 October 2008. He stated that he is too busy and that anything after that date sent to any address will not be signed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 April 2009, Starr reunited with McCartney at the David Lynch "Change Begins Within" Benefit Concert at <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a>. After separate performances from Starr and other artists, McCartney's set came last, and towards the end he announced "Billy Shears", whereupon Starr joined him to perform "With a Little Help from My Friends" and, with all performers, "<a href="/wiki/I_Saw_Her_Standing_There" title="I Saw Her Standing There">I Saw Her Standing There</a>" and "Cosmically Conscious".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr appeared on-stage during Microsoft's June 2009 <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Entertainment_Expo_2009" title="Electronic Entertainment Expo 2009">E3</a> press conference with Yoko Ono, McCartney and <a href="/wiki/Olivia_Harrison" title="Olivia Harrison">Olivia Harrison</a> to promote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles:_Rock_Band" title="The Beatles: Rock Band">The Beatles: Rock Band</a></i> video game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 2009, Starr once again performed the voice of Thomas the Tank Engine for "<a href="/wiki/The_Official_BBC_Children_in_Need_Medley" title="The Official BBC Children in Need Medley">The Official BBC Children in Need Medley</a>". This is the first number 1 UK hit Starr has been involved in since the Beatles disbanded in 1970 (not counting guest appearances on other singles by other artists).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span></h3>
<p>In 2010 Starr self-produced and released his fifteenth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Y_Not" title="Y Not">Y Not</a></i>, which included the track "<a href="/wiki/Walk_with_You" title="Walk with You">Walk with You</a>" and featured a vocal contribution from McCartney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> Later that year, he appeared during <i><a href="/wiki/Hope_for_Haiti_Now:_A_Global_Benefit_for_Earthquake_Relief" title="Hope for Haiti Now: A Global Benefit for Earthquake Relief">Hope for Haiti Now: A Global Benefit for Earthquake Relief</a></i> as a celebrity phone operator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday-clooneyexplains_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday-clooneyexplains-188"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> On 7 July 2010, Starr celebrated his 70th birthday at Radio City Music Hall, New York with another All-Starr Band concert, topped with friends and family joining him on stage including Yoko Ono and his son Zak: McCartney made a surprise appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr recorded a cover of <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a>'s "Think It Over" for the tribute album <i><a href="/wiki/Listen_to_Me:_Buddy_Holly" title="Listen to Me: Buddy Holly">Listen to Me: Buddy Holly</a></i>, which was released on 6 September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> On 30 January 2012, he released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_2012" title="Ringo 2012">Ringo 2012</a></i>. Later that year, Starr announced that his All-Starr Band would tour the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rim" title="Pacific Rim">Pacific Rim</a> during 2013 with select dates in New Zealand, Australia and Japan; it would be his first performance in Japan since 1996, and his debut in both New Zealand and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2014, Starr reunited with Paul McCartney for a special performance at the <a href="/wiki/56th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="56th Annual Grammy Awards">56th Annual Grammy Awards</a> performing the song "<a href="/wiki/Queenie_Eye" title="Queenie Eye">Queenie Eye</a>" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Staples_Centre" title="Staples Centre">Staples Centre</a> in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2014, Starr was featured alongside McCartney in the program <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_That_Changed_America:_A_Grammy_Salute_to_The_Beatles" title="The Night That Changed America: A Grammy Salute to The Beatles">The Night That Changed America: A Grammy Salute to The Beatles</a></i>.</p>
<p>In the summer of 2014, Starr toured Canada and the US with an updated version of the Twelfth All-Starr Band, featuring multi-instrumentalist <a href="/wiki/Warren_Ham" title="Warren Ham">Warren Ham</a> instead of saxophonist <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rivera" title="Mark Rivera">Mark Rivera</a>. In July 2014, Starr became involved in "#peacerocks", an anti-violence campaign started by fashion designer <a href="/wiki/John_Varvatos" title="John Varvatos">John Varvatos</a>, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/David_Lynch_Foundation" title="David Lynch Foundation">David Lynch Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-instyle7.2F14_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-instyle7.2F14-193"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwd_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwd-194"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2014, Starr won at the <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i> Men of the Year Awards for his humanitarian work with the David Lynch Foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015, through a Twitter post, Starr first revealed the title of his new 11-track studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Postcards_from_Paradise" title="Postcards from Paradise">Postcards from Paradise</a></i>, set for release on 31 March 2015. This title comes from one of the tracks of the album. The album comes just weeks in advance of Starr's induction into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>. Several album titles were considered, including "Let Love Lead", one of the 11 tracks.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicianship">Musicianship</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>
<p>During his youth, Starr had been a devoted fan of skiffle and <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> music, but by the time he joined the Texans in 1958, he had developed a preference for rock and roll.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpitz2005343.E2.80.93344_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpitz2005343.E2.80.93344-196"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> He was also influenced by <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> artists, including <a href="/wiki/Hank_Williams" title="Hank Williams">Hank Williams</a>, Buck Owens and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> drummers such as <a href="/wiki/Chico_Hamilton" title="Chico Hamilton">Chico Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yusef_Lateef" title="Yusef Lateef">Yusef Lateef</a>, whose compositional style inspired Starr's fluid and energetic drum fills and <a href="/wiki/Groove_(music)" title="Groove (music)">grooves</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> While reflecting on Buddy Rich, Starr commented: "He does things with one hand that I can't do with nine, but that's technique. Everyone I talk to says 'What about Buddy Rich?' Well, what about him? Because he doesn't turn me on."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200542_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200542-198"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> He stated that he "was never really into drummers", but identified <a href="/wiki/Cozy_Cole" title="Cozy Cole">Cozy Cole</a> '​s 1958 <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover</a> of <a href="/wiki/Benny_Goodman" title="Benny Goodman">Benny Goodman</a> '​s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Topsy_(song)" title="Topsy (song)">Topsy Part Two</a>" as "the one drum record" he bought.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr's first musical hero was <a href="/wiki/Gene_Autry" title="Gene Autry">Gene Autry</a>, about whom he commented: "I remember getting shivers up my back when he sang, "<a href="/wiki/South_of_the_Border_(1939_song)" title="South of the Border (1939 song)">South of the Border</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200520_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200520-200"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> By the early 1960s he had become an ardent fan of <a href="/wiki/Lee_Dorsey" title="Lee Dorsey">Lee Dorsey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200576_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200576-201"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> In November 1964, Starr told <i><a href="/wiki/Melody_Maker" title="Melody Maker">Melody Maker</a></i>: "Our music is second-hand versions of negro music ... Ninety per cent of the music I like is coloured."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005113_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005113-202"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drums">Drums</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg"><img alt="A colour photograph of Starr playing a dark coloured drum kit on a stage. The background is yellow." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2248" data-file-width="4000" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg/250px-20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg/375px-20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg/500px-20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20110626_043_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_drums_WP.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr with his All-Starr Band in Paris, 26 June 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The overall effect of Starr's drumming for the Beatles has received high praise from notable drummers. Starr commented: "I'm no good on the technical things ... I'm your basic offbeat drummer with funny fills ... because I'm really left-handed playing a right-handed kit. I can't roll around the drums because of that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200444_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200444-203"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Beatles producer George Martin stated: "Ringo hit good and hard and used the tom-tom well, even though he couldn't do a roll to save his life", although Martin later added, "He's got tremendous feel. He always helped us to hit the right tempo for a song, and gave it that support – that rock-solid back-beat – that made the recording of all the Beatles' songs that much easier."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200444_203-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200444-203"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr commented: "I've always believed that the drummer is not there to interpret the song", comparing his drumming to painting, he stated: "I am the foundation, and then I put a bit of glow here and there ... If there's a gap, I want to be good enough to fill it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200542_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200542-198"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, readers of <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine voted Starr as the fifth-greatest drummer of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> Journalist Robyn Flans, a long-time contributor with <i>Modern Drummer</i> magazine, writing for the Percussive Arts Society stated: "I cannot count the number of drummers who have told me that Ringo inspired their passion for drums".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAS_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-PAS-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Drummer <a href="/wiki/Steve_Smith_(musician)" title="Steve Smith (musician)">Steve Smith</a> commented on Starr's musical contribution:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Before Ringo, drum stars were measured by their soloing ability and virtuosity. Ringo's popularity brought forth a new paradigm in how the public saw drummers. We started to see the drummer as an equal participant in the compositional aspect. One of Ringo's great qualities was that he composed unique, stylistic drum parts for the Beatles' songs. His parts are so signature to the songs that you can listen to a Ringo drum part without the rest of the music and still identify the song.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAS_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-PAS-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Starr influenced Phil Collins,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-battistoni_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-battistoni-205"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> the drummer for <a href="/wiki/Genesis_(band)" title="Genesis (band)">Genesis</a>, who said: "I think he's vastly underrated, Ringo. The drum fills on "<a href="/wiki/A_Day_in_the_Life" title="A Day in the Life">A Day in the Life</a>" are very, very complex things. You could take a great drummer from today and say, 'I want it like that', and they really wouldn't know what to do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 1980, Lennon told <i>Rolling Stone</i>:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Ringo was a star in his own right in Liverpool before we even met. Ringo was a professional drummer who sang and performed and was in one of the top groups in Britain, but especially in Liverpool. So Ringo's talent would have come out one way or the other ... whatever that spark is in Ringo, we all know it but can't put our finger on it. Whether it's acting, drumming, or singing, I don't know. There's something in him that is projectable and he would have surfaced as an individual ... Ringo is a damn good drummer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In his extensive survey of the Beatles' recording sessions, historian <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lewisohn" title="Mark Lewisohn">Mark Lewisohn</a> confirmed that Starr was both proficient and remarkably reliable and consistent. According to Lewisohn, there were fewer than a dozen occasions in the Beatles' eight-year recording career where session breakdowns were caused by Starr making a mistake, while the vast majority of takes were stopped owing to mistakes by the other three Beatles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn198895_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn198895-208"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr is considered to have influenced various modern drumming techniques, such as the <a href="/wiki/Matched_grip" title="Matched grip">matched grip</a>, tuning the drums lower, and using muffling devices on tonal rings, as well as placing the drums on high risers for visibility as part of the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PAS_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-PAS-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Ken Micallef and Donnie Marshall, co-authors of <i>Classic Rock Drummers</i>: "Ringo's fat tom sounds and delicate cymbal work were imitated by thousands of drummers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to his drumming with the Beatles, Starr performs nearly all of his own drums on his solo records.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocals">Vocals</span></h3>
<p>Starr sang lead vocals for a song on most of the Beatles' studio albums as part of an attempt to establish a vocal personality for each band member. In many cases, Lennon or McCartney wrote the lyrics and melody especially for him, as they did for "Yellow Submarine" from <i>Revolver</i> and "With a Little Help from My Friends" on <i>Sgt. Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harddayswritelittlehelp_210-0"><a href="#cite_note-harddayswritelittlehelp-210"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup> These melodies were tailored to Starr's limited <a href="/wiki/Baritone" title="Baritone">baritone</a> vocal range. Because of his distinctive voice, Starr rarely performed backing vocals during his time with the Beatles, but they can be heard on songs such as "Maxwell's Silver Hammer" and "Carry That Weight".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999252:_.22Maxwell.27s_Silver_Hammer.22.2C_268:_.22Carry_That_Weight.22_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999252:_.22Maxwell.27s_Silver_Hammer.22.2C_268:_.22Carry_That_Weight.22-211"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> He is also the lead vocalist on his compositions "Don't Pass Me By" and "Octopus's Garden".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEverett1999206:_.22Don.27t_Pass_Me_By.22.2C_254.E2.80.93255:_.22Octopus.27s_Garden.22_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEverett1999206:_.22Don.27t_Pass_Me_By.22.2C_254.E2.80.93255:_.22Octopus.27s_Garden.22-212"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, he sang lead on "I Wanna Be Your Man", "Boys", "Matchbox", "Honey Don't", "Act Naturally", "Good Night" and "<a href="/wiki/What_Goes_On_(Beatles_song)" title="What Goes On (Beatles song)">What Goes On</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songwriting">Songwriting</span></h3>
<p>Starr's idiosyncratic turns of phrase, or <i>Ringoisms</i> as they became known, such as <i><a href="/wiki/A_Hard_Day%27s_Night_(song)#Title" title="A Hard Day's Night (song)">a hard day's night</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Knows" title="Tomorrow Never Knows">tomorrow never knows</a></i>, were used as song titles by the Beatles, particularly by Lennon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry20043_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry20043-214"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> McCartney commented: "Ringo would do these little <a href="/wiki/Malapropism" title="Malapropism">malapropisms</a>, he would say things slightly wrong, like people do, but his were always wonderful, very lyrical ... they were sort of magic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles1997164_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles1997164-215"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> As well as inspiring his bandmates' creativity in this way, Starr occasionally contributed lyrics to unfinished Lennon–McCartney songs, such as the line "darning his socks in the night when there's nobody there" from "<a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Rigby" title="Eleanor Rigby">Eleanor Rigby</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harddayswriteeleanorrigby_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-harddayswriteeleanorrigby-216"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr is credited as a co-writer of "What Goes On", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flying_(Beatles_song)" title="Flying (Beatles song)">Flying</a>" and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dig_It_(The_Beatles_song)" title="Dig It (The Beatles song)">Dig It</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>nb 14<span>]</span></a></sup> On material issued after the break-up, Starr received a writing credit for "Taking a Trip to Carolina" and received joint songwriting credits with the other three Beatles for "<a href="/wiki/12-Bar_Original" title="12-Bar Original">12-Bar Original</a>", "Los Paranoias", "<a href="/wiki/Christmas_Time_(Is_Here_Again)" title="Christmas Time (Is Here Again)">Christmas Time (Is Here Again)</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suzy_Parker_(Beatles_Song)" title="Suzy Parker (Beatles Song)">Suzy Parker</a>", heard in the <i>Let It Be</i> film, and "Jessie's Dream" from the <i>Magical Mystery Tour</i> film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnterberger2006134:_.2212-Bar_Original.22.2C_181:_.22Jessie.27s_Dream.22.2C_185.E2.80.93186:_.22Christmas_Time_.28Is_Here_Again.29.22.2C_215:_.22Los_Paranoias.22.2C_236:_.22Taking_a_Trip_to_Carolina.22.2C_244:_.22Suzy_Parker.22_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnterberger2006134:_.2212-Bar_Original.22.2C_181:_.22Jessie.27s_Dream.22.2C_185.E2.80.93186:_.22Christmas_Time_.28Is_Here_Again.29.22.2C_215:_.22Los_Paranoias.22.2C_236:_.22Taking_a_Trip_to_Carolina.22.2C_244:_.22Suzy_Parker.22-220"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr has also written or co-written a large amount of his solo material, but has stated that he only started being heavily involved in the writing process during the production of 1998's <i><a href="/wiki/Vertical_Man" title="Vertical Man">Vertical Man</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>When Starr married Maureen in 1965, Beatles manager Brian Epstein served as <a href="/wiki/Groomsman#Best_man" title="Groomsman">best man</a>, with Starr's step-father Harry Graves and fellow Beatle George Harrison as witnesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup> Soon afterwards, the couple's matrimony became the subject of a US <a href="/wiki/Novelty_song" title="Novelty song">novelty song</a>, "Treat Him Tender, Maureen", by the Chicklettes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005142_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005142-222"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr and Maureen had three children together: <a href="/wiki/Zak_Starkey" title="Zak Starkey">Zak</a> (born 13 September 1965), Jason (born 19 August 1967) and <a href="/wiki/Lee_Starkey" title="Lee Starkey">Lee</a> (born 11 November 1970).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004322.E2.80.93325_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004322.E2.80.93325-223"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1971, Starr purchased Lennon's former home, <a href="/wiki/Tittenhurst_Park" title="Tittenhurst Park">Tittenhurst Park</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sunninghill,_Berkshire" title="Sunninghill, Berkshire">Sunninghill</a> in Berkshire and moved his family there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorman2008615_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorman2008615-224"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Following Starr's repeated infidelities, the couple divorced in 1975.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> Maureen died from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leukaemia" title="Leukaemia">leukaemia</a> in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005362_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005362-226"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1980, while on the set of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Caveman_(film)" title="Caveman (film)">Caveman</a></i>, Starr met actress <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bach" title="Barbara Bach">Barbara Bach</a>; they were married on 27 April 1981.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005291.E2.80.93292.2C_304_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005291.E2.80.93292.2C_304-227"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1985, he was the first of the Beatles to become a grandfather upon the birth of Zak's daughter, Tatia Jayne Starkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Name_of_Zak_Starkey.27s_daughter_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-Name_of_Zak_Starkey.27s_daughter-228"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> Zak Starkey is also a drummer, and during his father's regular absences, he spent time with <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Keith_Moon" title="Keith Moon">Keith Moon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005281_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005281-229"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> Zak has performed with his father during some All-Starr Band tours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005374.E2.80.93375_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005374.E2.80.93375-230"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr and Bach split their time between homes in <a href="/wiki/Cranleigh" title="Cranleigh">Cranleigh, Surrey</a>; Los Angeles; and <a href="/wiki/Monte_Carlo" title="Monte Carlo">Monte Carlo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004162_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004162-231"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_Rich_List_2011" title="Sunday Times Rich List 2011">Sunday Times Rich List 2011</a></i>, Starr was listed at number 56 with an estimated personal wealth of £150 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, Starr was estimated to be the wealthiest drummer in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014 Starr announced that his 200-acre Surrey estate at Rydinghurst, with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grade_II" title="Grade II">Grade II</a> listed <a href="/wiki/Jacobean_architecture" title="Jacobean architecture">Jacobean</a> house, was for sale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_recognition">Awards and recognition</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg"><img alt="A colour photograph of Starr wearing sunglasses and singing into a microphone. The background is blue and purple." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2248" data-file-width="4000" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg/220px-20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg/330px-20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg/440px-20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20110626_102_All-Starr-Band-in-Paris_Ringo-Starr_WP.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Starr in Paris, June 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_the_Beatles" title="List of awards and nominations received by the Beatles">List of awards and nominations received by the Beatles</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1965_Birthday_Honours" title="1965 Birthday Honours">1965 Birthday Honours</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, Starr and the other Beatles were appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Members of the Order of the British Empire">Members of the Order of the British Empire</a> (MBE);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELondon_Gazette19655487.E2.80.935489_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELondon_Gazette19655487.E2.80.935489-236"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> they received their insignia from the Queen at an <a href="/wiki/Investiture" title="Investiture">investiture</a> at Buckingham Palace on 26 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> He and the other Beatles were cumulatively nominated for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Newcomer" title="BAFTA Award for Best Newcomer">BAFTA Award for Best Newcomer</a> for their performances in the 1964 film <i>A Hard Day's Night</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1971, the Beatles received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> for Best Original Song Score for the film <i>Let It Be</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200696_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthallPerry200696-239"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1988, the Beatles were inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004297.E2.80.93298_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004297.E2.80.93298-240"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards" title="50th Grammy Awards">50th Grammy Awards</a>, Starr, George Martin, and his son <a href="/wiki/Giles_Martin" title="Giles Martin">Giles</a> accepted the Best Compilation Soundtrack award for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Love_(The_Beatles_album)" title="Love (The Beatles album)">Love</a></i>. On 9 November 2008, Starr accepted a Diamond Award on behalf of the Beatles during the 2008 <a href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards" title="World Music Awards">World Music Awards</a> ceremony in Monaco.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The minor planet <a href="/wiki/4150_Starr" title="4150 Starr">4150 Starr</a>, discovered on 31 August 1984 by <a href="/wiki/Brian_A._Skiff" title="Brian A. Skiff">Brian A. Skiff</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Mesa_Station" title="Anderson Mesa Station">Anderson Mesa Station</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Lowell_Observatory" title="Lowell Observatory">Lowell Observatory</a>, was named in Starr's honour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harvard-planet_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harvard-planet-241"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr was nominated for a 1989 <a href="/wiki/Daytime_Emmy_Award" title="Daytime Emmy Award">Daytime Emmy Award</a> for Outstanding Performer in a Children's Series for his role as Mr. Conductor in the television series <i>Shining Time Station</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIngham2009143_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIngham2009143-242"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> On 8 February 2010, he was honoured with the 2,401st star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a> by the Hollywood Chamber of Commerce. It is located at 1750 North Vine Street, in front of the <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Records" title="Capitol Records">Capitol Records</a> building, as are the stars for Lennon, McCartney and Harrison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr was awarded the <i><a href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)" title="Mojo (magazine)">Mojo</a></i> Icon in recognition of his music career in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_2011_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_2011-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> He became <i>Commandeur</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Ordre_des_Arts_et_des_Lettres" title="Ordre des Arts et des Lettres">Ordre des Arts et des Lettres</a> in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014 it was announced that Starr would be inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a> class of 2015 for Musical Excellence, making him the last member of The Beatles separately inducted into the Hall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RRHF_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-RRHF-245"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_career">Film career</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr_filmography" title="Ringo Starr filmography">Ringo Starr filmography</a></div>
<p>Starr has received praise from critics and movie industry professionals regarding his acting; director and producer <a href="/wiki/Walter_Shenson" title="Walter Shenson">Walter Shenson</a> called him "a superb actor, an absolute natural."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005125_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005125-75"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> By the mid-1960s, Starr had become a connoisseur of film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005125.2C_145_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005125.2C_145-246"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition to his roles in <i>A Hard Day's Night</i> (1964), <i>Help!</i> (1965), <i>Magical Mystery Tour</i> (1967), and <i>Let It Be</i> (1970), Starr also acted in <i><a href="/wiki/Candy_(1968_film)" title="Candy (1968 film)">Candy</a></i> (1968), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Christian_(film)" title="The Magic Christian (film)">The Magic Christian</a></i> (1969), <i><a href="/wiki/Blindman" title="Blindman">Blindman</a></i> (1971), <i><a href="/wiki/Son_of_Dracula_(1974_film)" title="Son of Dracula (1974 film)">Son of Dracula</a></i> (1974) and <i><a href="/wiki/Caveman_(film)" title="Caveman (film)">Caveman</a></i> (1981).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200499.E2.80.93100:_.27.27Candy.27.27.3B_244.E2.80.93245:_.27.27The_Magic_Christian.27.27.3B_88.E2.80.9389:_.27.27Blindman.27.27.3B_316.E2.80.93317:_.27.27Son_of_Dracula.27.27.3B_106.E2.80.93108:_.27.27Caveman.27.27_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200499.E2.80.93100:_.27.27Candy.27.27.3B_244.E2.80.93245:_.27.27The_Magic_Christian.27.27.3B_88.E2.80.9389:_.27.27Blindman.27.27.3B_316.E2.80.93317:_.27.27Son_of_Dracula.27.27.3B_106.E2.80.93108:_.27.27Caveman.27.27-247"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1971, he starred as Larry the Dwarf in <a href="/wiki/Frank_Zappa" title="Frank Zappa">Frank Zappa</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/200_Motels" title="200 Motels">200 Motels</a></i> and was featured in Harry Nilsson's animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Point!" title="The Point!">The Point!</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004268:_.27.27The_Point.21.27.27.2C_373:_.27.27200_Motels.27.27_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004268:_.27.27The_Point.21.27.27.2C_373:_.27.27200_Motels.27.27-248"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup> He co-starred in <i><a href="/wiki/That%27ll_Be_the_Day_(film)" title="That'll Be the Day (film)">That'll Be the Day</a></i> (1973) as a <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Boy" title="Teddy Boy">Teddy Boy</a> and appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Waltz" title="The Last Waltz">The Last Waltz</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> documentary film about the 1976 farewell concert of <a href="/wiki/The_Band" title="The Band">the Band</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004235:_.27.27The_Last_Waltz.27.27.2C_331:_.27.27That.27ll_Be_the_Day.27.27_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004235:_.27.27The_Last_Waltz.27.27.2C_331:_.27.27That.27ll_Be_the_Day.27.27-249"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Starr played The Pope in <a href="/wiki/Ken_Russell" title="Ken Russell">Ken Russell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Lisztomania_(film)" title="Lisztomania (film)">Lisztomania</a></i> (1975), and a fictionalised version of himself in McCartney's <i><a href="/wiki/Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street_(film)" title="Give My Regards to Broad Street (film)">Give My Regards to Broad Street</a></i> in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004206:_.27.27Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street.27.27.3B_236:_.27.27Lisztomania.27.27_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004206:_.27.27Give_My_Regards_to_Broad_Street.27.27.3B_236:_.27.27Lisztomania.27.27-250"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr appeared as himself and a downtrodden alter-ego Ognir Rrats in <i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_(1978_film)" title="Ringo (1978 film)">Ringo</a></i> (1978), an American-made television comedy film based loosely on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prince_and_the_Pauper" title="The Prince and the Pauper">The Prince and the Pauper</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004281.E2.80.93282:_.27.27The_Prince_and_the_Pauper.27.27_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004281.E2.80.93282:_.27.27The_Prince_and_the_Pauper.27.27-251"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> For the 1979 documentary film on the Who, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kids_Are_Alright_(film)" title="The Kids Are Alright (film)">The Kids Are Alright</a></i>, Starr appeared in interview segments with fellow drummer Keith Moon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr_discography" title="Ringo Starr discography">Ringo Starr discography</a></div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_discography" title="The Beatles discography">The Beatles discography</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_recorded_by_Ringo_Starr" title="List of songs recorded by Ringo Starr">List of songs recorded by Ringo Starr</a></div>
<p>Since the breakup of the Beatles, Starr has released 17 solo studio albums:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Sentimental_Journey_(Ringo_Starr_album)" title="Sentimental Journey (Ringo Starr album)">Sentimental Journey</a></i> (1970)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Beaucoups_of_Blues" title="Beaucoups of Blues">Beaucoups of Blues</a></i> (1970)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ringo_(album)" title="Ringo (album)">Ringo</a></i> (1973)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Goodnight_Vienna" title="Goodnight Vienna">Goodnight Vienna</a></i> (1974)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Ringo%27s_Rotogravure" title="Ringo's Rotogravure">Ringo's Rotogravure</a></i> (1976)</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">His paternal grandfather was born with the surname "<a href="/wiki/Parkin_(surname)" title="Parkin (surname)">Parkin</a>", and later adopted his stepfather's surname, "Starkey".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDavies2009141_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDavies2009141-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Starr had first drummed with the Texans on 25 March 1959, at the Mardi Gras club in Liverpool.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-51">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Of the nine <a href="/wiki/Gramophone_record" title="Gramophone record">78-rpm disks</a> that were cut only one is known to have survived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199223_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199223-50"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Starr sat in for an ill Pete Best during two shows on 5 February 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004110_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004110-54"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-64">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Martin chose the 4 September version of "Love Me Do" with Starr on drums for the A-side and the 11 September recording of "P.S. I Love You" with Starr on maracas for the B-side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259_56-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisohn199259-56"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Epstein then accompanied Nicol to the Melbourne airport where he gave him a cheque and a gold Eterna-matic wrist watch inscribed: "From the Beatles and Brian Epstein to Jimmy – with appreciation and gratitude."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004255_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004255-84"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Starr had his tonsils removed later that year during a Christmas holiday.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry2004111_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry2004111-85"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Starr offered no suggestions for inclusion on the album's historic front cover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005160_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005160-100"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-113"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-113">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Starr compared his stay in India with a Butlins camp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGould2007463.E2.80.93468_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGould2007463.E2.80.93468-111"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> His childhood health problems had an enduring effect in the form of allergies and sensitivities to food, and when the Beatles travelled to India he took his own food with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-128"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-128">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During filming he became friends with T. Rex frontman <a href="/wiki/Marc_Bolan" title="Marc Bolan">Marc Bolan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200491.E2.80.9393_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200491.E2.80.9393-127"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1975, these singles and others were included on Starr's first greatest hits compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/Blast_from_Your_Past" title="Blast from Your Past">Blast from Your Past</a></i>, which was the last album released by Apple Records.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200487.E2.80.9388_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200487.E2.80.9388-136"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-149">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1981, Harrison included the single on his album <i><a href="/wiki/Somewhere_in_England" title="Somewhere in England">Somewhere in England</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarry200317.E2.80.9318.2C_349.E2.80.93350.2C_367_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarry200317.E2.80.9318.2C_349.E2.80.93350.2C_367-148"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-161"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-161">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Starr experienced his first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackout_(alcohol-related_amnesia)" title="Blackout (alcohol-related amnesia)">alcoholic blackout</a> at the age of nine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson200524_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson200524-160"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-182"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-182">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The album's production credits read, "Produced by Ringo Starr and Mark Hudson; Re-Produced by Ringo Starr and David Stewart." All of the songs but one were written with members of the Roundheads, although Stewart also has several co-writing credits.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-219"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-219">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"What Goes On" was a pre-Beatles Lennon song to which McCartney added a middle eight in an effort to provide Starr a lead vocal on <i>Rubber Soul</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEClayson2005_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEClayson2005-218"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="background: #EEDD82">1934–1940</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
